<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="contentSub2"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Classical-era composer (1756–1791)</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"Mozart" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Mozart_(disambiguation)" title="Mozart (disambiguation)">Mozart (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Croce-Mozart-Detail.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="748" data-file-width="577" decoding="async" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Croce-Mozart-Detail.jpg/220px-Croce-Mozart-Detail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Croce-Mozart-Detail.jpg/330px-Croce-Mozart-Detail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Croce-Mozart-Detail.jpg/440px-Croce-Mozart-Detail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Croce-Mozart-Detail.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozart, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;"> 1781</span>, detail from portrait by <a href="/wiki/Johann_Nepomuk_della_Croce" title="Johann Nepomuk della Croce">Johann Nepomuk della Croce</a> <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_Signature.svg"><img alt="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart Signature.svg" data-file-height="125" data-file-width="563" decoding="async" height="49" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_Signature.svg/220px-Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_Signature.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_Signature.svg/330px-Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_Signature.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_Signature.svg/440px-Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_Signature.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a></div></div></div>
<p><b>Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[n 1]</a></sup> (27 January 1756 – 5 December 1791), baptised as <b>Joannes Chrysostomus Wolfgangus Theophilus Mozart</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[n 2]</a></sup> was a prolific and influential composer of the <a href="/wiki/Classical_period_(music)" title="Classical period (music)">Classical period</a>. Despite his short life, his rapid pace of composition resulted in more than <a href="/wiki/List_of_compositions_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="List of compositions by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">800 works</a> of virtually every genre of his time. Many of these compositions are acknowledged as pinnacles of the <a href="/wiki/Symphony" title="Symphony">symphonic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Concerto" title="Concerto">concertante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chamber_music" title="Chamber music">chamber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">operatic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Choir" title="Choir">choral</a> repertoire. Mozart is widely regarded as among the greatest composers in the history of Western music,<sup class="reference" id='cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBuch2017"Introduction"_3-0'><a href='#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBuch2017"Introduction"-3'>[1]</a></sup> with his music admired for its "melodic beauty, its formal elegance and its richness of harmony and texture".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEisenSadie2001_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEisenSadie2001-4">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Prince-Archbishopric_of_Salzburg" title="Prince-Archbishopric of Salzburg">Salzburg</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, Mozart showed prodigious ability from his earliest childhood. Already competent on <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_instrument" title="Keyboard instrument">keyboard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Violin" title="Violin">violin</a>, he composed from the age of five and performed before European royalty. His father took him on a <a href="/wiki/Mozart_family_grand_tour" title="Mozart family grand tour">grand tour</a> of Europe and then <a href="/wiki/Mozart_in_Italy" title="Mozart in Italy">three trips to Italy</a>. At 17, he was a musician at the Salzburg court but grew restless and travelled in search of a better position.
</p><p>While visiting <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> in 1781, Mozart was dismissed from his Salzburg position. He stayed in Vienna, where he achieved fame but little financial security. During his final years there, he composed many of his best-known <a href="/wiki/List_of_symphonies_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="List of symphonies by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">symphonies</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_compositions_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart#Concertos" title="List of compositions by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">concertos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_operas_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="List of operas by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">operas</a>. His <a href="/wiki/Requiem_(Mozart)" title="Requiem (Mozart)">Requiem</a> was largely unfinished by the time of his death at the age of 35, the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Death of Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">circumstances of which</a> are uncertain and much mythologized.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="866" data-file-width="566" decoding="async" height="275" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg/180px-Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg/270px-Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg/360px-Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozart's birthplace at Getreidegasse 9, Salzburg</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_and_childhood">Family and childhood</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_name" title="Mozart's name">Mozart's name</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozart_family" title="Mozart family">Mozart family</a></div>
<p>Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart was born on 27 January 1756 to <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Mozart" title="Leopold Mozart">Leopold Mozart</a> (1719–1787) and <a href="/wiki/Anna_Maria_Mozart" title="Anna Maria Mozart">Anna Maria</a>, née Pertl (1720–1778), at <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_birthplace" title="Mozart's birthplace">Getreidegasse 9</a> in <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[3]</a></sup> Salzburg was the capital of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Salzburg" title="Archbishopric of Salzburg">Archbishopric of Salzburg</a>, an ecclesiastic principality in the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> (today in <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[n 3]</a></sup> He was the youngest of seven children, five of whom died in infancy. His elder sister was <a href="/wiki/Maria_Anna_Mozart" title="Maria Anna Mozart">Maria Anna Mozart</a> (1751–1829), nicknamed "Nannerl". Mozart was baptised the day after his birth, at <a href="/wiki/Salzburg_Cathedral" title="Salzburg Cathedral">St. Rupert's Cathedral</a> in Salzburg. The baptismal record gives his name in Latinized form, as <i>Joannes Chrysostomus Wolfgangus Theophilus Mozart</i>. He generally called himself "Wolfgang Amadè Mozart"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutsch19659_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutsch19659-7">[4]</a></sup> as an adult, but <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_name" title="Mozart's name">his name</a> had many variants.
</p><p>Leopold Mozart, a native of <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon199521_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon199521-8">[5]</a></sup> then an Imperial Free City in the Holy Roman Empire, was a minor composer and an experienced teacher. In 1743, he was appointed as the fourth violinist in the musical establishment of Count <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Anton_von_Firmian" title="Leopold Anton von Firmian">Leopold Anton von Firmian</a>, the ruling <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Salzburg#Prince-Bishopric_(1213–1803)" title="Archbishopric of Salzburg">Prince-Archbishop of Salzburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEisenSadie2001_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEisenSadie2001-4">[2]</a></sup> Four years later, he married Anna Maria in Salzburg. Leopold became the orchestra's deputy <a href="/wiki/Kapellmeister" title="Kapellmeister">Kapellmeister</a> in 1763. During the year of his son's birth, Leopold published a violin textbook, <i><a href="/wiki/Versuch_einer_gr%C3%BCndlichen_Violinschule" title="Versuch einer gründlichen Violinschule">Versuch einer gründlichen Violinschule</a></i>, which achieved success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon199532_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon199532-9">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>When Nannerl was 7, she began keyboard lessons with her father, while her three-year-old brother looked on. Years later, after her brother's death, she reminisced:
</p>
<blockquote><p>He often spent much time at the <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_instrument" title="Keyboard instrument">clavier</a>, picking out thirds, which he was ever striking, and his pleasure showed that it sounded good.<span class="nowrap"> </span>... In the fourth year of his age his father, for a game as it were, began to teach him a few minuets and pieces at the clavier.<span class="nowrap"> </span>... He could play it faultlessly and with the greatest delicacy, and keeping exactly in time.<span class="nowrap"> </span>... At the age of five, he was already composing little pieces, which he played to his father who wrote them down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutsch1965455_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutsch1965455-10">[7]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louis_Carrogis_dit_Carmontelle_-_Portrait_de_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_(Salzbourg,_1756-Vienne,_1791)_jouant_%C3%A0_Paris_avec_son_p%C3%A8re_Jean..._-_Google_Art_Project.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5203" data-file-width="3322" decoding="async" height="266" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Louis_Carrogis_dit_Carmontelle_-_Portrait_de_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_%28Salzbourg%2C_1756-Vienne%2C_1791%29_jouant_%C3%A0_Paris_avec_son_p%C3%A8re_Jean..._-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/170px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Louis_Carrogis_dit_Carmontelle_-_Portrait_de_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_%28Salzbourg%2C_1756-Vienne%2C_1791%29_jouant_%C3%A0_Paris_avec_son_p%C3%A8re_Jean..._-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/255px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Louis_Carrogis_dit_Carmontelle_-_Portrait_de_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_%28Salzbourg%2C_1756-Vienne%2C_1791%29_jouant_%C3%A0_Paris_avec_son_p%C3%A8re_Jean..._-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/340px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louis_Carrogis_dit_Carmontelle_-_Portrait_de_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_(Salzbourg,_1756-Vienne,_1791)_jouant_%C3%A0_Paris_avec_son_p%C3%A8re_Jean..._-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Mozart family on tour: Leopold, Wolfgang, and Nannerl. Watercolour by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Carrogis_Carmontelle" title="Louis Carrogis Carmontelle">Carmontelle</a>, c.<span class="nowrap"> </span>1763<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon199544_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon199544-11">[8]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>These early pieces, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6chel_catalogue" title="Köchel catalogue">K.</a> 1–5, were recorded in the <i><a href="/wiki/Nannerl_Notenbuch" title="Nannerl Notenbuch">Nannerl Notenbuch</a></i>. There is some scholarly debate about whether Mozart was four or five years old when he created his first musical compositions, though there is little doubt that Mozart composed his first three pieces of music within a few weeks of each other: K. 1a, 1b, and 1c.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[9]</a></sup>
</p><p>In his early years, Wolfgang's father was his only teacher. Along with music, he taught his children languages and academic subjects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_39_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_39-13">[10]</a></sup> Solomon notes that, while Leopold was a devoted teacher to his children, there is evidence that Mozart was keen to progress beyond what he was taught.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_39_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_39-13">[10]</a></sup> His first ink-spattered composition and his precocious efforts with the violin were of his initiative and came as a surprise to Leopold,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutsch1965453_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutsch1965453-14">[11]</a></sup> who eventually gave up composing when his son's musical talents became evident.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon199533_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon199533-15">[12]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="1762.E2.80.9373:_Travel"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1762–73:_Travel">1762–73: Travel</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mozart_family_grand_tour" title="Mozart family grand tour">Mozart family grand tour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozart_in_Italy" title="Mozart in Italy">Mozart in Italy</a></div>
<p>While Wolfgang was young, his family made several European journeys in which he and Nannerl performed as <a href="/wiki/Child_prodigy" title="Child prodigy">child prodigies</a>. These began with an exhibition in 1762 at the court of <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">Prince-elector</a> <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_III_Joseph,_Elector_of_Bavaria" title="Maximilian III Joseph, Elector of Bavaria">Maximilian III</a> of Bavaria in Munich, and at the Imperial Courts in Vienna and Prague. A long concert tour followed, spanning three and a half years, taking the family to the courts of Munich, <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a>, Paris, London,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[13]</a></sup> Dover, The Hague, Amsterdam, Utrecht, <a href="/wiki/Mechelen" title="Mechelen">Mechelen</a> and again to Paris, and back home via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zurich" title="Zurich">Zurich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donaueschingen" title="Donaueschingen">Donaueschingen</a>, and Munich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGrove1954926_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGrove1954926-17">[14]</a></sup> During this trip, Wolfgang met many musicians and acquainted himself with the works of other composers. A particularly significant influence was <a href="/wiki/Johann_Christian_Bach" title="Johann Christian Bach">Johann Christian Bach</a>, whom he visited in London in 1764 and 1765. When he was eight years old, Mozart wrote <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._1_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 1 (Mozart)">his first symphony</a>, most of which was probably transcribed by his father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[15]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_at_the_age_of_13_in_Verona,_1770.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3061" data-file-width="2475" decoding="async" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Portrait_of_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_at_the_age_of_13_in_Verona%2C_1770.jpg/220px-Portrait_of_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_at_the_age_of_13_in_Verona%2C_1770.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Portrait_of_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_at_the_age_of_13_in_Verona%2C_1770.jpg/330px-Portrait_of_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_at_the_age_of_13_in_Verona%2C_1770.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Portrait_of_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_at_the_age_of_13_in_Verona%2C_1770.jpg/440px-Portrait_of_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_at_the_age_of_13_in_Verona%2C_1770.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_at_the_age_of_13_in_Verona,_1770.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozart aged 14 in January 1770 (School of Verona, attributed to <a href="/wiki/Giambettino_Cignaroli" title="Giambettino Cignaroli">Giambettino Cignaroli</a>)</div></div></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097025294">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096940132">.mw-parser-output .listen .side-box-text{line-height:1.1em}.mw-parser-output .listen-plain{border:none;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded{width:100%;margin:0;border-width:1px 0 0 0;background:transparent}.mw-parser-output .listen-header{padding:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen-embedded .listen-header{padding:2px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen-file-header{padding:4px 0}.mw-parser-output .listen .description{padding-top:2px}.mw-parser-output .listen .mw-tmh-player{max-width:100%}@media(max-width:719px){.mw-parser-output .listen{clear:both}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .listen:not(.listen-noimage){width:320px}.mw-parser-output .listen-left{overflow:visible;float:left}.mw-parser-output .listen-center{float:none;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}}</style><div class="side-box side-box-right listen noprint">

<div class="description">Composed 9 October 1770 for admission to the <a href="/wiki/Accademia_Filarmonica_di_Bologna" title="Accademia Filarmonica di Bologna">Accademia Filarmonica di Bologna</a>; Performed by Phillip W. Serna, treble, tenor &amp; bass <a href="/wiki/Viol" title="Viol">viols</a></div></div></div></div>
<div class="side-box-abovebelow"><hr/><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></div>
</div>
<p>The family trips were often challenging, and travel conditions were primitive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalliwell199851,_53_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalliwell199851,_53-19">[16]</a></sup> They had to wait for invitations and reimbursement from the nobility, and they endured long, near-fatal illnesses far from home: first Leopold (London, summer 1764),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalliwell199882–83_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalliwell199882–83-20">[17]</a></sup> then both children (The Hague, autumn 1765).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalliwell199899–102_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalliwell199899–102-21">[18]</a></sup> The family again went to Vienna in late 1767 and remained there until December 1768.
</p><p>After one year in Salzburg, Leopold and Wolfgang set off for Italy, leaving Anna Maria and Nannerl at home. This tour lasted from December 1769 to March 1771. As with earlier journeys, Leopold wanted to display his son's abilities as a performer and a rapidly maturing composer. Wolfgang met <a href="/wiki/Josef_Myslive%C4%8Dek" title="Josef Mysliveček">Josef Mysliveček</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Martini" title="Giovanni Battista Martini">Giovanni Battista Martini</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bologna" title="Bologna">Bologna</a> and was accepted as a member of the famous <a href="/wiki/Accademia_Filarmonica_di_Bologna" title="Accademia Filarmonica di Bologna">Accademia Filarmonica</a>. In Rome, he heard <a href="/wiki/Gregorio_Allegri" title="Gregorio Allegri">Gregorio Allegri</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Miserere_(Allegri)" title="Miserere (Allegri)">Miserere</a></i> twice in performance, in the <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel" title="Sistine Chapel">Sistine Chapel</a>, and wrote it out from memory, thus producing the first unauthorized copy of this closely guarded property of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Vatican</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Milan, Mozart wrote the opera <i><a href="/wiki/Mitridate,_re_di_Ponto" title="Mitridate, re di Ponto">Mitridate, re di Ponto</a></i> (1770), which was performed with success. This led to further opera <a href="/wiki/Commission_(art)" title="Commission (art)">commissions</a>. He returned with his father twice to Milan (August–December 1771; October 1772 – March 1773) for the composition and premieres of <i><a href="/wiki/Ascanio_in_Alba" title="Ascanio in Alba">Ascanio in Alba</a></i> (1771) and <i><a href="/wiki/Lucio_Silla" title="Lucio Silla">Lucio Silla</a></i> (1772). Leopold hoped these visits would result in a professional appointment for his son, and indeed ruling <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Karl,_Archduke_of_Austria-Este" title="Ferdinand Karl, Archduke of Austria-Este">Archduke Ferdinand</a> contemplated hiring Mozart, but owing to his mother <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa" title="Maria Theresa">Empress Maria Theresa</a>'s reluctance to employ "useless people", the matter was dropped<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[n 4]</a></sup> and Leopold's hopes were never realized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998172,_183–185_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998172,_183–185-25">[21]</a></sup> Toward the end of the journey, Mozart wrote the solo <a href="/wiki/Motet" title="Motet">motet</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Exsultate,_jubilate" title="Exsultate, jubilate">Exsultate, jubilate</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6chel_catalogue" title="Köchel catalogue">K.</a> 165.
</p>
<h3><span id="1773.E2.80.9377:_Employment_at_the_Salzburg_court"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1773–77:_Employment_at_the_Salzburg_court">1773–77: Employment at the Salzburg court</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3536" data-file-width="2320" decoding="async" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg/170px-Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg/255px-Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg/340px-Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzmeisterhaus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tanzmeisterhaus (page does not exist)">Tanzmeisterhaus</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanzmeisterhaus" title="de:Tanzmeisterhaus">de</a>]</span>, Salzburg, Mozart family residence from 1773; reconstructed 1996</div></div></div>
<p>After finally returning with his father from Italy on 13 March 1773, Mozart was employed as a court musician by the ruler of Salzburg, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hieronymus_von_Colloredo_(1732%E2%80%931812)" title="Hieronymus von Colloredo (1732–1812)">Prince-Archbishop Hieronymus Colloredo</a>. The composer had many friends and admirers in Salzburg<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995106_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995106-26">[22]</a></sup> and had the opportunity to work in many genres, including symphonies, sonatas, string quartets, <a href="/wiki/Mass_(music)" title="Mass (music)">masses</a>, serenades, and a few minor operas. Between April and December 1775, Mozart developed an enthusiasm for violin concertos, producing a series of five (the only ones he ever wrote), which steadily increased in their musical sophistication. The last three—<a href="/wiki/Violin_Concerto_No._3_(Mozart)" title="Violin Concerto No. 3 (Mozart)">K. 216</a>, <a href="/wiki/Violin_Concerto_No._4_(Mozart)" title="Violin Concerto No. 4 (Mozart)">K. 218</a>, <a href="/wiki/Violin_Concerto_No._5_(Mozart)" title="Violin Concerto No. 5 (Mozart)">K. 219</a>—are now staples of the repertoire. In 1776, he turned his efforts to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mozart_piano_concertos" title="Mozart piano concertos">piano concertos</a>, culminating in the E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">♭</span></span> concerto <a href="/wiki/Piano_Concerto_No._9_(Mozart)" title="Piano Concerto No. 9 (Mozart)">K. 271</a> of early 1777, considered by critics to be a breakthrough work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995103_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995103-27">[23]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite these artistic successes, Mozart grew increasingly discontented with Salzburg and redoubled his efforts to find a position elsewhere. One reason was his low salary, 150 florins a year;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon199598_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon199598-28">[24]</a></sup> Mozart longed to compose operas, and Salzburg provided only rare occasions for these. The situation worsened in 1775 when the court theatre was closed, especially since the other theatre in Salzburg was primarily reserved for visiting troupes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995107_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995107-29">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>Two long expeditions in search of work interrupted this long Salzburg stay. Mozart and his father visited Vienna from 14 July to 26 September 1773, and Munich from 6<span class="nowrap"> </span>December 1774 to March 1775. Neither visit was successful, though the Munich journey resulted in a popular success with the premiere of Mozart's opera <i><a href="/wiki/La_finta_giardiniera" title="La finta giardiniera">La finta giardiniera</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995109_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995109-30">[26]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1777.E2.80.9378:_Journey_to_Paris"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1777–78:_Journey_to_Paris">1777–78: Journey to Paris</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="510" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg/180px-Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg/270px-Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg/360px-Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozart wearing the badge of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Golden_Spur" title="Order of the Golden Spur">Order of the Golden Spur</a> which he received in 1770 from <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_XIV" title="Pope Clement XIV">Pope Clement XIV</a> in Rome. The painting is a 1777 copy of a work now lost.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVatican1770_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVatican1770-31">[27]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In August 1777, Mozart resigned his position at Salzburg<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998225_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998225-32">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[n 5]</a></sup> and on 23 September ventured out once more in search of employment, with visits to <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a>, Mannheim, Paris, and Munich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESadie1998_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESadie1998-34">[29]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart became acquainted with members of the <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_school" title="Mannheim school">famous orchestra</a> in Mannheim, the best in Europe at the time. He also fell in love with <a href="/wiki/Aloysia_Weber" title="Aloysia Weber">Aloysia Weber</a>, one of four daughters of a musical family. There were prospects of employment in Mannheim, but they came to nothing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[30]</a></sup> and Mozart left for Paris on 14 March 1778<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutsch1965174_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutsch1965174-36">[31]</a></sup> to continue his search. One of his letters from Paris hints at a possible post as an organist at <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Versailles" title="Palace of Versailles">Versailles</a>, but Mozart was not interested in such an appointment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995149_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995149-37">[32]</a></sup> He fell into debt and took to pawning valuables.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998304–305_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998304–305-38">[33]</a></sup> The nadir of the visit occurred when Mozart's mother was taken ill and died on 3<span class="nowrap"> </span>July 1778.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbert2007509_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbert2007509-39">[34]</a></sup> There had been delays in calling a doctor—probably, according to Halliwell, because of a lack of funds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998305_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998305-40">[35]</a></sup> Mozart stayed with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Melchior_Grimm" title="Melchior Grimm">Melchior Grimm</a>, who, as a personal secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Louis_Philippe_I,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Louis Philippe I, Duke of Orléans">Duke d'Orléans</a>, lived in his mansion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>While Mozart was in Paris, his father was pursuing opportunities of employment for him in Salzburg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998chs._18–19_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998chs._18–19-42">[37]</a></sup> With the support of the local nobility, Mozart was offered a post as court organist and concertmaster. The annual salary was 450 florins,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995157_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995157-43">[38]</a></sup> but he was reluctant to accept.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998322_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHalliwell1998322-44">[39]</a></sup> By that time, relations between Grimm and Mozart had cooled, and Mozart moved out. After leaving Paris in September 1778 for Strasbourg, he lingered in Mannheim and Munich, still hoping to obtain an appointment outside Salzburg. In Munich, he again encountered Aloysia, now a very successful singer, but she was no longer interested in him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_3_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_3-45">[40]</a></sup> Mozart finally returned to Salzburg on 15 January 1779 and took up his new appointment, but his discontent with Salzburg remained undiminished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>Among the better-known works which Mozart wrote on the Paris journey are the <a href="/wiki/Piano_Sonata_No._8_(Mozart)" title="Piano Sonata No. 8 (Mozart)">A minor piano sonata</a>, K. 310/300d, the <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._31_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 31 (Mozart)">"Paris" Symphony</a> (No. 31), which were performed in Paris on 12 and 18 June 1778;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeutsch1965176_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeutsch1965176-47">[42]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Concerto_for_Flute,_Harp,_and_Orchestra_(Mozart)" title="Concerto for Flute, Harp, and Orchestra (Mozart)">Concerto for Flute and Harp</a> in C major, K. 299/297c.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEinstein1965276–277_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEinstein1965276–277-48">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vienna">Vienna</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1781:_Departure">1781: Departure</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1520" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg/220px-Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg/330px-Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg/440px-Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mozart_family" title="Mozart family">Mozart family</a>, c. 1780 (<a href="/wiki/Johann_Nepomuk_della_Croce" title="Johann Nepomuk della Croce">della Croce</a>); the portrait on the wall is of Mozart's mother.</div></div></div>
<p>In January 1781, Mozart's opera <i><a href="/wiki/Idomeneo" title="Idomeneo">Idomeneo</a></i> premiered with "considerable success" in Munich.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESadie1980vol._12,_p._700_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESadie1980vol._12,_p._700-49">[44]</a></sup> The following March, Mozart was summoned to Vienna, where his employer, Archbishop Colloredo, was attending the celebrations for the accession of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph II</a> to the Austrian throne. For Colloredo, this was simply a matter of wanting his musical servant to be at hand (Mozart indeed was required to dine in Colloredo's establishment with the valets and cooks).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[n 6]</a></sup> He planned a bigger career as he continued in the archbishop's service;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpaethling2000238_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpaethling2000238-52">[46]</a></sup> for example, he wrote to his father:
</p>
<blockquote><p>My main goal right now is to meet the emperor in some agreeable fashion, I am absolutely determined he <em>should get to know me</em>. I would be so happy if I could whip through my opera for him and then play a fugue or two, for that's what he likes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spaethling237_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Spaethling237-53">[47]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Mozart did indeed soon meet the Emperor, who eventually was to support his career substantially with commissions and a part-time position.
</p><p>In the same letter to his father just quoted, Mozart outlined his plans to participate as a soloist in the concerts of the <i><a href="/wiki/Tonk%C3%BCnstler-Societ%C3%A4t" title="Tonkünstler-Societät">Tonkünstler-Societät</a></i>, a prominent benefit concert series;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spaethling237_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Spaethling237-53">[47]</a></sup> this plan as well came to pass after the local nobility prevailed on Colloredo to drop his opposition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpaethling2000238–239_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpaethling2000238–239-54">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>Colloredo's wish to prevent Mozart from performing outside his establishment was in other cases carried through, raising the composer's anger; one example was a chance to perform before the Emperor at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_Wilhelmine_Thun" title="Maria Wilhelmine Thun">Countess Thun</a>'s for a fee equal to half of his yearly Salzburg salary.
</p><p>The quarrel with the archbishop came to a head in May: Mozart attempted to resign and was refused. The following month, permission was granted, but in a grossly insulting way: the composer was dismissed literally "with a kick in the arse", administered by the archbishop's steward, Count Arco. Mozart decided to settle in Vienna as a freelance performer and composer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_4_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_4-55">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>The quarrel with Colloredo was more difficult for Mozart because his father sided against him. Hoping fervently that he would obediently follow Colloredo back to Salzburg, Mozart's father exchanged intense letters with his son, urging him to be reconciled with their employer. Mozart passionately defended his intention to pursue an independent career in Vienna. The debate ended when Mozart was dismissed by the archbishop, freeing himself both of his employer and of his father's demands to return. Solomon characterizes Mozart's resignation as a "revolutionary step" that significantly altered the course of his life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995247_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995247-56">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Haydn_and_Mozart" title="Haydn and Mozart">Haydn and Mozart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozart_and_Freemasonry" title="Mozart and Freemasonry">Mozart and Freemasonry</a></div>
<p>Mozart's new career in Vienna began well. He often performed as a pianist, notably in a competition before the Emperor with <a href="/wiki/Muzio_Clementi" title="Muzio Clementi">Muzio Clementi</a> on 24 December 1781,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_4_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_4-55">[49]</a></sup> and he soon "had established himself as the finest keyboard player in Vienna".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_4_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_4-55">[49]</a></sup> He also prospered as a composer, and in 1782 completed the opera <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Entf%C3%BChrung_aus_dem_Serail" title="Die Entführung aus dem Serail">Die Entführung aus dem Serail</a></i> ("The Abduction from the Seraglio"), which premiered on 16 July 1782 and achieved considerable success. The work was soon being performed "throughout German-speaking Europe",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_4_55-3"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_4-55">[49]</a></sup> and thoroughly established Mozart's reputation as a composer.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Constanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="749" data-file-width="556" decoding="async" height="229" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Constanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg/170px-Constanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Constanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg/255px-Constanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Constanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg/340px-Constanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Constanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1782 portrait of <a href="/wiki/Constanze_Mozart" title="Constanze Mozart">Constanze Mozart</a> by her brother-in-law <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lange" title="Joseph Lange">Joseph Lange</a></div></div></div>
<p>Near the height of his quarrels with Colloredo, Mozart moved in with the Weber family, who had moved to Vienna from Mannheim. The family's father, Fridolin, had died, and the Webers were now taking in lodgers to make ends meet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995253_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995253-57">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_and_children">Marriage and children</span></h4>
<p>After failing to win the hand of Aloysia Weber, who was now married to the actor and artist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lange" title="Joseph Lange">Joseph Lange</a>, Mozart's interest shifted to the third daughter of the family, <a href="/wiki/Constanze_Mozart" title="Constanze Mozart">Constanze</a>.
</p><p>The courtship did not go entirely smoothly; surviving correspondence indicates that Mozart and Constanze briefly separated in April 1782.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995259_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995259-58">[52]</a></sup> Mozart faced a challenging task in getting his father's permission for the marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sol258_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sol258-59">[53]</a></sup> The couple were finally married on 4<span class="nowrap"> </span>August 1782 in <a href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Cathedral,_Vienna" title="St. Stephen's Cathedral, Vienna">St. Stephen's Cathedral</a>, the day before his father's consenting letter arrived in the mail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sol258_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sol258-59">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>The couple had six children, of whom only two survived infancy:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995265–266_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995265–266-60">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Raimund Leopold (17 June – 19 August 1783)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karl_Thomas_Mozart" title="Karl Thomas Mozart">Karl Thomas Mozart</a> (21 September 1784 – 31 October 1858)</li>
<li>Johann Thomas Leopold (18 October – 15 November 1786)</li>
<li>Theresia Constanzia Adelheid Friedericke Maria Anna (27 December 1787 – 29 June 1788)</li>
<li>Anna Maria (died soon after birth, 16 November 1789)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Wolfgang_Mozart" title="Franz Xaver Wolfgang Mozart">Franz Xaver Wolfgang Mozart</a> (26 July 1791 – 29 July 1844)</li></ul>
<h3><span id="1782.E2.80.9387"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1782–87">1782–87</span></h3>
<p>In 1782 and 1783, Mozart became intimately acquainted with the work of <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Johann Sebastian Bach</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Frideric_Handel" title="George Frideric Handel">George Frideric Handel</a> as a result of the influence of <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_van_Swieten" title="Gottfried van Swieten">Gottfried van Swieten</a>, who owned many manuscripts of the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">Baroque</a> masters. Mozart's study of these scores inspired compositions in Baroque style and later influenced his musical language, for example in <a href="/wiki/Fugue" title="Fugue">fugal</a> passages in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Flute" title="The Magic Flute">Die Zauberflöte</a></i> ("The Magic Flute") and the finale of <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._41_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 41 (Mozart)">Symphony No. 41</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEisenSadie2001_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEisenSadie2001-4">[2]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1783, Mozart and his wife visited his family in Salzburg. His father and sister were cordially polite to Constanze, but the visit prompted the composition of one of Mozart's great liturgical pieces, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Mass_in_C_minor" title="Great Mass in C minor">Mass in C minor</a>. Though not completed, it was premiered in Salzburg, with Constanze singing a solo part.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995270_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995270-61">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart met <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Haydn" title="Joseph Haydn">Joseph Haydn</a> in Vienna around 1784, and the two composers became friends. When Haydn visited Vienna, they sometimes played together in an impromptu <a href="/wiki/String_quartet" title="String quartet">string quartet</a>. Mozart's <a href="/wiki/Haydn_Quartets_(Mozart)" title="Haydn Quartets (Mozart)">six quartets dedicated to Haydn</a> (K. 387, K. 421, K. 428, K. 458, K. 464, and K. 465) date from the period 1782 to 1785, and are judged to be a response to <a href="/wiki/String_Quartets,_Op._33_(Haydn)" title="String Quartets, Op. 33 (Haydn)">Haydn's Opus 33</a> set from 1781.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[56]</a></sup> Haydn wrote, "posterity will not see such a talent again in 100 years"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELandon1990171_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELandon1990171-63">[57]</a></sup> and in 1785 told Mozart's father: "I tell you before God, and as an honest man, your son is the greatest composer known to me by person and repute, he has taste and what is more the greatest skill in composition."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1782 to 1785 Mozart mounted concerts with himself as a soloist, presenting three or four new piano concertos in each season. Since space in the theatres was scarce, he booked unconventional venues: a large room in the Trattnerhof apartment building, and the ballroom of the Mehlgrube restaurant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_293_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_293-65">[59]</a></sup> The concerts were very popular, and <a href="/wiki/Piano_concertos_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Piano concertos by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">his concertos</a> premiered there are still firm fixtures in his repertoire. Solomon writes that during this period, Mozart created "a harmonious connection between an eager composer-performer and a delighted audience, which was given the opportunity of witnessing the transformation and perfection of a major musical genre".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_293_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_293-65">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>With substantial returns from his concerts and elsewhere, Mozart and his wife adopted a more luxurious lifestyle. They moved to an expensive apartment, with a yearly rent of 460 florins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_298_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_298-66">[60]</a></sup> Mozart bought a fine <a href="/wiki/Fortepiano" title="Fortepiano">fortepiano</a> from <a href="/wiki/Anton_Walter" title="Anton Walter">Anton Walter</a> for about 900 florins, and a <a href="/wiki/Carom_billiards" title="Carom billiards">billiard</a> table for about 300.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_298_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_298-66">[60]</a></sup> The Mozarts sent their son <a href="/wiki/Karl_Thomas_Mozart" title="Karl Thomas Mozart">Karl Thomas</a> to an expensive boarding school<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995430_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995430-67">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995578_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995578-68">[62]</a></sup> and kept servants. During this period Mozart saved little of his income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995§27_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995§27-69">[63]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995431_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995431-70">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 December 1784, Mozart became a <a href="/wiki/Freemasonry" title="Freemasonry">Freemason</a>, admitted to the lodge Zur Wohltätigkeit ("Beneficence").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995321_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995321-71">[65]</a></sup> Freemasonry played an essential role in the remainder of Mozart's life: he attended meetings, a number of his friends were Masons, and on various occasions, he composed Masonic music, e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Maurerische_Trauermusik" title="Maurerische Trauermusik">Maurerische Trauermusik</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[66]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="1786.E2.80.9387:_Return_to_opera"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1786–87:_Return_to_opera">1786–87: Return to opera</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg/170px-Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg/255px-Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg/340px-Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fortepiano" title="Fortepiano">Fortepiano</a> played by Mozart in 1787, Czech Museum of Music, Prague<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[67]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Despite the great success of <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Entf%C3%BChrung_aus_dem_Serail" title="Die Entführung aus dem Serail">Die Entführung aus dem Serail</a></i>, Mozart did little operatic writing for the next four years, producing only two unfinished works and the one-act <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Schauspieldirektor" title="Der Schauspieldirektor">Der Schauspieldirektor</a></i>. He focused instead on his career as a piano soloist and writer of concertos. Around the end of 1785, Mozart moved away from keyboard writing<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harvnb|Solomon|1995_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-harvnb|Solomon|1995-74">[68]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2010)">page needed</span></a></i>]</sup> and began his famous operatic collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/Libretto" title="Libretto">librettist</a> <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Da_Ponte" title="Lorenzo Da Ponte">Lorenzo Da Ponte</a>. The year 1786 saw the successful premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marriage_of_Figaro" title="The Marriage of Figaro">The Marriage of Figaro</a></i> in Vienna. Its reception in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mozart_and_Prague" title="Mozart and Prague">Prague</a> later in the year was even warmer, and this led to a second collaboration with Da Ponte: the opera <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Giovanni" title="Don Giovanni">Don Giovanni</a></i>, which premiered in October 1787 to acclaim in Prague, but less success in Vienna during 1788.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFreeman2021131–168_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFreeman2021131–168-75">[69]</a></sup> The two are among Mozart's most famous works and are mainstays of operatic repertoire today, though at their premieres their musical complexity caused difficulty both for listeners and for performers. These developments were not witnessed by Mozart's father, who had died on 28 May 1787.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[70]</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 1787, Mozart finally obtained a steady post under aristocratic patronage. Emperor Joseph II appointed him as his "chamber composer", a post that had fallen vacant the previous month on the death of <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Willibald_Gluck" title="Christoph Willibald Gluck">Gluck</a>. It was a part-time appointment, paying just 800 florins per year, and required Mozart only to compose dances for the annual balls in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hofburg_Palace" title="Hofburg Palace">Redoutensaal</a> (see <i><a href="/wiki/Mozart_and_dance" title="Mozart and dance">Mozart and dance</a></i>). This modest income became important to Mozart when hard times arrived. Court records show that Joseph aimed to keep the esteemed composer from leaving Vienna in pursuit of better prospects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_423_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_423-77">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[n 7]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1787, the young <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a> spent several weeks in Vienna, hoping to study with Mozart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHaberl2006215–255_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHaberl2006215–255-79">[72]</a></sup> No reliable records survive to indicate whether the <a href="/wiki/Beethoven_and_Mozart" title="Beethoven and Mozart">two composers</a> ever met.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_years">Later years</span></h3>
<h4><span id="1788.E2.80.9390"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1788–90">1788–90</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_Berlin_journey" title="Mozart's Berlin journey">Mozart's Berlin journey</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="558" data-file-width="499" decoding="async" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg/170px-Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg/255px-Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg/340px-Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Drawing of Mozart in <a href="/wiki/Silverpoint" title="Silverpoint">silverpoint</a>, made by <a href="/wiki/Dora_Stock" title="Dora Stock">Dora Stock</a> during Mozart's visit to Dresden, April 1789</div></div></div>
<p>Toward the end of the decade, Mozart's circumstances worsened. Around 1786 he had ceased to appear frequently in public concerts, and his income shrank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_6_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_6-80">[73]</a></sup> This was a difficult time for musicians in Vienna because of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Turkish_War_(1787%E2%80%931791)" title="Austro-Turkish War (1787–1791)">Austro-Turkish War</a>: both the general level of prosperity and the ability of the aristocracy to support music had declined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harvnb|Solomon|1995_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-harvnb|Solomon|1995-74">[68]</a></sup>
</p><p>By mid-1788, Mozart and his family had moved from central Vienna to the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Alsergrund" title="Alsergrund">Alsergrund</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_6_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_6-80">[73]</a></sup> Although it has been suggested that Mozart aimed to reduce his rental expenses by moving to a suburb, as he wrote in his letter to <a href="/wiki/Michael_von_Puchberg" title="Michael von Puchberg">Michael von Puchberg</a>, Mozart had not reduced his expenses but merely increased the housing space at his disposal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELorenz2010_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELorenz2010-81">[74]</a></sup> Mozart began to borrow money, most often from his friend and fellow mason Puchberg; "a pitiful sequence of letters pleading for loans" survives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESadie1980vol._12,_p._710_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESadie1980vol._12,_p._710-82">[75]</a></sup> Maynard Solomon and others have suggested that Mozart was suffering from depression, and it seems his musical output slowed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESteptoe1990208_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESteptoe1990208-83">[76]</a></sup> Major works of the period include the last three symphonies (Nos. <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._39_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 39 (Mozart)">39</a>, <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._40_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 40 (Mozart)">40</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._41_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 41 (Mozart)">41</a>, all from 1788), and the last of the three Da Ponte operas, <i><a href="/wiki/Cos%C3%AC_fan_tutte" title="Così fan tutte">Così fan tutte</a></i>, premiered in 1790.
</p><p>Around this time, Mozart made some long journeys hoping to improve his fortunes, visiting Leipzig, Dresden, and Berlin in the spring of 1789, and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, Mannheim, and other German cities in 1790.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1791">1791</span></h4>
<p>Mozart's last year was, until his final illness struck, a time of high productivity—and by some accounts, one of personal recovery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995§30_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995§30-84">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[n 8]</a></sup> He composed a great deal, including some of his most admired works: the opera <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Flute" title="The Magic Flute">The Magic Flute</a></i>; the final piano concerto (<a href="/wiki/Piano_Concerto_No._27_(Mozart)" title="Piano Concerto No. 27 (Mozart)">K. 595 in B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">♭</span></span></a>); the <a href="/wiki/Clarinet_Concerto_(Mozart)" title="Clarinet Concerto (Mozart)">Clarinet Concerto</a> K. 622; the last in his series of string quintets (<a href="/wiki/String_Quintet_No._6_(Mozart)" title="String Quintet No. 6 (Mozart)">K. 614 in E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">♭</span></span></a>); the motet <a href="/wiki/Ave_verum_corpus_(Mozart)" title="Ave verum corpus (Mozart)">Ave verum corpus</a> K. 618; and the unfinished <a href="/wiki/Requiem_(Mozart)" title="Requiem (Mozart)">Requiem</a> K. 626.
</p><p>Mozart's financial situation, a source of anxiety in 1790, finally began to improve. Although the evidence is inconclusive,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_477_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_477-86">[78]</a></sup> it appears that wealthy patrons in Hungary and Amsterdam pledged annuities to Mozart in return for the occasional composition. He is thought to have benefited from the sale of dance music written in his role as Imperial chamber composer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_477_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_477-86">[78]</a></sup> Mozart no longer borrowed large sums from Puchberg and began to pay off his debts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_477_86-2"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_477-86">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>He experienced great satisfaction in the public success of some of his works, notably <i>The Magic Flute</i> (which was performed several times in the short period between its premiere and Mozart's death)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995487_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995487-87">[79]</a></sup> and the Little Masonic Cantata K. 623, premiered on 17 November 1791.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[80]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_illness_and_death">Final illness and death</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Death of Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Death of Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1784" data-file-width="1392" decoding="async" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg/170px-Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg/255px-Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg/340px-Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Posthumous painting by <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Krafft" title="Barbara Krafft">Barbara Krafft</a> in 1819</div></div></div><p>Mozart fell ill while in Prague for the premiere, on 6<span class="nowrap"> </span>September 1791, of his opera <i><a href="/wiki/La_clemenza_di_Tito" title="La clemenza di Tito">La clemenza di Tito</a></i>, which was written in that same year on commission for Emperor <a href="/wiki/Leopold_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Leopold II, Holy Roman Emperor">Leopold II</a>'s coronation festivities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFreeman2021193–230_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFreeman2021193–230-89">[81]</a></sup> He continued his professional functions for some time and conducted the premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Flute" title="The Magic Flute">The Magic Flute</a></i> on 30 September. His health deteriorated on 20 November, at which point he became bedridden, suffering from swelling, pain, and vomiting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995491_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995491-90">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart was nursed in his final days by his wife and her youngest sister, and was attended by the family doctor, Thomas Franz Closset. He was mentally occupied with the task of finishing his <a href="/wiki/Requiem_(Mozart)" title="Requiem (Mozart)">Requiem</a>, but the evidence that he dictated passages to his student <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_S%C3%BCssmayr" title="Franz Xaver Süssmayr">Franz Xaver Süssmayr</a> is minimal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995493,_588_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995493,_588-91">[83]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart died in his home on 5 December 1791<span style="display:none">(1791-12-05)</span> (aged 35) at 12:55 am.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[84]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Grove_Dictionary_of_Music_and_Musicians" title="The New Grove Dictionary of Music and Musicians">New Grove</a></i> describes his funeral:
</p>
<blockquote><p>Mozart was interred in a common grave, in accordance with contemporary Viennese custom, at the <a href="/wiki/St._Marx_Cemetery" title="St. Marx Cemetery">St. Marx Cemetery</a> outside the city on 7<span class="nowrap"> </span>December. If, as later reports say, no mourners attended, that too is consistent with Viennese burial customs at the time; later <a href="/wiki/Otto_Jahn" title="Otto Jahn">Otto Jahn</a> (1856) wrote that <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Salieri" title="Antonio Salieri">Salieri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_S%C3%BCssmayr" title="Franz Xaver Süssmayr">Süssmayr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_van_Swieten" title="Gottfried van Swieten">van Swieten</a> and two other musicians were present. The tale of a storm and snow is false; the day was calm and mild.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESadie1980vol._12,_p._716_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESadie1980vol._12,_p._716-93">[85]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The expression "common grave" refers to neither a communal grave nor a pauper's grave, but an individual grave for a member of the common people (i.e., not the aristocracy). Common graves were subject to excavation after ten years; the graves of aristocrats were not.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>The cause of Mozart's death is not known with certainty. The official record of <i>hitziges Frieselfieber</i> ("severe miliary fever", referring to a rash that looks like <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet seeds</a>) is more a symptomatic description than a diagnosis. Researchers have suggested more than a hundred causes of death, including acute <a href="/wiki/Rheumatic_fever" title="Rheumatic fever">rheumatic fever</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wakin_2010_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wakin_2010-95">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Streptococcus" title="Streptococcus">streptococcal</a> <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infection</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[90]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trichinosis" title="Trichinosis">trichinosis</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[92]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercury_poisoning" title="Mercury poisoning">mercury poisoning</a>, and a rare <a href="/wiki/Nephrology" title="Nephrology">kidney</a> ailment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wakin_2010_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wakin_2010-95">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart's modest funeral did not reflect his standing with the public as a composer; memorial services and concerts in Vienna and Prague were well-attended. Indeed, in the period immediately after his death, his reputation rose substantially. Solomon describes an "unprecedented wave of enthusiasm"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Solomonp499_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Solomonp499-101">[93]</a></sup> for his work; <a href="/wiki/Biographies_of_Mozart" title="Biographies of Mozart">biographies were written</a> first by <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Schlichtegroll" title="Friedrich Schlichtegroll">Schlichtegroll</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Niemetschek" title="Franz Xaver Niemetschek">Niemetschek</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georg_Nikolaus_von_Nissen" title="Georg Nikolaus von Nissen">Nissen</a>, and publishers vied to produce complete editions of his works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Solomonp499_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Solomonp499-101">[93]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearance_and_character">Appearance and character</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mozart_(unfinished)_by_Lange_1782.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="550" data-file-width="567" decoding="async" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg/220px-Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg/330px-Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg/440px-Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mozart_(unfinished)_by_Lange_1782.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Detail of portrait of Mozart by his brother-in-law Joseph Lange</div></div></div>
<p>Mozart's physical appearance was described by tenor <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kelly_(tenor)" title="Michael Kelly (tenor)">Michael Kelly</a> in his <i>Reminiscences</i>: "a remarkably small man, very thin and pale, with a profusion of fine, fair hair of which he was rather vain". His early biographer Niemetschek wrote, "there was nothing special about [his] physique.<span class="nowrap"> </span>... He was small and his countenance, except for his large intense eyes, gave no signs of his genius." His facial complexion was pitted, a reminder of his <a href="/wiki/Mozart_and_smallpox" title="Mozart and smallpox">childhood case of smallpox</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-102">[94]</a></sup> Of his voice, his wife later wrote that it "was a tenor, rather soft in speaking and delicate in singing, but when anything excited him, or it became necessary to exert it, it was both powerful and energetic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995308_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995308-103">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>He loved elegant clothing. Kelly remembered him at a rehearsal: <span class="nowrap">"[He]</span> was on the stage with his crimson <a href="/wiki/Pelisse" title="Pelisse">pelisse</a> and gold-laced <a href="/wiki/Bicorne" title="Bicorne">cocked hat</a>, giving the time of the music to the orchestra." Based on pictures that researchers were able to find of Mozart, he seemed to wear a white wig for most of his formal occasions—researchers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salzburg_Mozarteum" title="Salzburg Mozarteum">Salzburg Mozarteum</a> declared that only one of his fourteen portraits they had found showed him without his wig.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph-102">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart usually worked long and hard, finishing compositions at a tremendous pace as deadlines approached. He often made sketches and drafts; unlike Beethoven's, these are mostly not preserved, as his wife sought to destroy them after his death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995310_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995310-104">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart lived at the center of the Viennese musical world, and knew a significant number and variety of people: fellow musicians, theatrical performers, fellow Salzburgers, and aristocrats, including some acquaintance with Emperor <a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph II</a>. Solomon considers his three closest friends to have been Gottfried von Jacquin, Count August Hatzfeld, and Sigmund Barisani; others included his elder colleague <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Haydn" title="Joseph Haydn">Joseph Haydn</a>, singers <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Gerl" title="Franz Xaver Gerl">Franz Xaver Gerl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benedikt_Schack" title="Benedikt Schack">Benedikt Schack</a>, and the horn player <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Leutgeb" title="Joseph Leutgeb">Joseph Leutgeb</a>. Leutgeb and Mozart carried on a curious kind of friendly mockery, often with Leutgeb as the butt of Mozart's <a href="/wiki/Practical_joke" title="Practical joke">practical jokes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995§20_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995§20-105">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>He enjoyed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billiards" title="Billiards">billiards</a>, dancing, and kept pets, including a canary, a <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_starling" title="Mozart's starling">starling</a>, a dog, and a horse for recreational riding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995319_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995319-106">[98]</a></sup> He had a startling fondness for <a href="/wiki/Mozart_and_scatology" title="Mozart and scatology">scatological humour</a>, which is preserved in his surviving letters, notably those written to his cousin <a href="/wiki/Maria_Anna_Thekla_Mozart" title="Maria Anna Thekla Mozart">Maria Anna Thekla Mozart</a> around 1777–1778, and in his correspondence with his sister and parents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995169_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995169-107">[99]</a></sup> Mozart also wrote scatological music, a series of <a href="/wiki/Canon_(music)" title="Canon (music)">canons</a> that he sang with his friends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[100]</a></sup> Mozart <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_and_the_Catholic_Church" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart and the Catholic Church">was raised a Catholic</a> and remained a devout member of the Church throughout his life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAbert2007[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidl6I6BwTMJ3sCpgPA743_743]_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAbert2007[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidl6I6BwTMJ3sCpgPA743_743]-110">[102]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Works.2C_musical_style.2C_and_innovations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Works,_musical_style,_and_innovations">Works, musical style, and innovations</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_compositions_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="List of compositions by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">List of compositions by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_operas_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="List of operas by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">List of operas by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_compositional_method" title="Mozart's compositional method">Mozart's compositional method</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Style">Style</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097025294" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096940132" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="side-box side-box-right listen noprint">
<div class="side-box-flex">
